Titles&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/h5&gt;&lt;div class="_5pcp"&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;span class="fsm fwn fcg"&gt;&lt;a class="_5pcq" href="/HighlandTitlesNatureReserve/posts/716927308430518" target=""&gt;&lt;abbr title="Wednesday, June 24, 2015 at 5:09am" data-utime="1435147798" data-shorten="1" class="_5ptz timestamp livetimestamp"&gt;11 hrs&lt;/abbr&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;span&gt;&lt;a data-hover="tooltip" aria-label="Show edit history" class="uiLinkSubtle" ajaxify="/ajax/edits/browser/post/?content_token=716927308430518" rel="dialog" href="#" data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;+E&quot;&#125;" role="button"&gt;Edited&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;a data-hover="tooltip" aria-label="Public" class="uiStreamPrivacy inlineBlock fbStreamPrivacy fbPrivacyAudienceIndicator _5pcq" href="#" role="button"&gt;&lt;i class="lock img sp_T1ZsogA4Y5H sx_4be06a"&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="_5pbx userContent" data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;K&quot;&#125;"&gt;&lt;div id="id_558b461fbd6e64288084446" class="text_exposed_root"&gt;&lt;p&gt;The Scottish Parliament yesterday unveiled its proposals to change the way that land is managed and owned in Scotland. This follows a period of consultation on the Future of Land Reform in Scotland, to which Highland Titles contributed.&lt;br /&gt; We believe that land is an essential Scottish resource which is currently in the hands of too few people - 432 people own half the land in Scotland. The use of land must support the common good. Highland Titles believes that the Land Reform Bi&lt;span class="text_exposed_hide"&gt;...&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="text_exposed_show"&gt;ll is overdue, welcome, and opens the way to making progress on the way Scotland is owned.&lt;br /&gt; Disappointingly, the Bill does not implement one of the proposals in the earlier consultation to make it possible to register title to souvenir land. Given the popularity of owning small plots of land, the benefits that this brings to local causes and communities and the relative simplicity of recording the transfer of ownership, this omission is lamentable.&lt;br /&gt; The bill introduces three substantial reforms. Firstly there will be a new right-to-buy power for communities, secondly non-domestic rates will apply to sporting estates and agricultural tenancy law will be changed, creating a Tenant Farming Commissioner as part of a Scottish Land Commission&lt;br /&gt; Taxing land devoted to shooting and deer forests is a positive step, removing a curious exemption from business rates which is hard to justify. If it helps cause the break-up of these great estates, making more land available for community enterprises such as Highland Titles, this would be very welcome.&lt;br /&gt; The Improvements to both systems of common good land and right to roam are welcome, as are the modest measures relating to charities.&lt;br /&gt; Scotland looks to be a better place because of the bill, despite its significant omission on souvenir land. Highland Titles welcomes the bill as a work in progress.&lt;br /&gt; The introduction of the Bill is a significant step forward in ensuring our land is used in the public interest and to the benefit of the people of Scotland. It will also end the stop start nature of land reform in Scotland that has limited progress.&quot;; Land Reform Minister, Dr. Aileen McLeod&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;span class="text_exposed_hide"&gt; data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;K&quot;&#125;"&gt;&lt;p&gt;Our SpyCams have 12 high power AA batteries tucked inside, which sounds a lot... but they have to power a pair of motion sensors, a video camera and if it&#039;s dusk or dark, an infra-red light. Normally you get a wee bit of notice as they start to run down, but a number of false readings, and therefore recordings, at night, had obviously zapped this set.&lt;br /&gt; What started out as an amazing capture turned into a 10 second grab... I could have wept! &lt;span&gt;&lt;a data-hover="tooltip" aria-label="Show edit history" class="uiLinkSubtle" ajaxify="/ajax/edits/browser/post/?content_token=716547525135163" rel="dialog" href="#" data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;+E&quot;&#125;" role="button"&gt;Edited&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;a data-hover="tooltip" aria-label="Public" class="uiStreamPrivacy inlineBlock fbStreamPrivacy fbPrivacyAudienceIndicator _5pcq" href="#" role="button"&gt;&lt;i class="lock img sp_T1ZsogA4Y5H sx_4be06a"&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="_5pbx userContent" data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;K&quot;&#125;"&gt;&lt;div id="id_558b461fbe2788310311472" class="text_exposed_root"&gt;&lt;p&gt;Would you like to Track A Gannet (T.A.G)?  This is a new and experimental project offering an unrivaled insight into the life-cycle of Britains largest native seabird, the Northern Gannet.  Highland Titles have adopted one gannet, Laird Glencoe, to help follow the feeding routes of these magnificent birds in real time.  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; T.A.G is jointly run by Britains smallest Wildlife Trust, the Alderney Wildlife Trust (AWT), the British Trust for Ornithology (BTO) and University of Live&lt;span class="text_exposed_hide"&gt;...&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="text_exposed_show"&gt;rpool, various sponsors, including Highland Titles. It has enabled gannets to be under constant surveillance using the  3G mobile network.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="text_exposed_show"&gt;&lt;p&gt;     Find where Laird Glencoe is at any time.  Follow the feeding routes of other birds in real time on the map (click the link below).  Please note the tags update every time they come within range of a 3G mobile network, and may be limited by solar battery charge.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;     Help us discover more about these beautiful and enigmatic birds as they forage throughout the English Channel in search of fish to raise their young.  Please post your comments, insights and updates at &#064;AlderneyWT.       &lt;a data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;*J&quot;&#125;" class="_3ekx"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="_42ef"&gt;&lt;span _ohf"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="mtm plm _5pcm"&gt;&lt;div class="mbs _11dd fwn fcg" data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;C&quot;&#125;"&gt;&lt;div class="_5pcn fwb" data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;k&quot;&#125;"&gt;&lt;a href="/scottishhighlandtitles/videos/921543797892265/?fref=nf"&gt;Highland Titles&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="mtm _5pco" data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;K&quot;&#125;"&gt;&lt;div id="id_558b461fbee397529171737" class="text_exposed_root"&gt;&lt;p&gt;Night badger capture up at the Jubilee Wood SpyCam.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; This big, black-and-white-headed woodland dweller is widely recognised, but much less often seen. &lt;br /&gt; Tufts of &lt;span class="text_exposed_hide"&gt;...&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="text_exposed_show"&gt;coarse grey or black hair on fence wires and posts and beside well-worn animal tracks are clues to badger presence. &lt;br /&gt; The badger is the largest British member of the family that includes pine marten, weasel, stoat and polecat, all of which have fairly strong body odours. &lt;br /&gt; Badgers keep a low profile through much of the winter, holed-up in their underground setts. Boars (males) roam to look for sows (females) in March, and cubs could be coming out from setts on summer evenings from June onwards.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;span class="text_exposed_hide"&gt; data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;K&quot;&#125;"&gt;&lt;div id="id_558b461fbf8612c92922313" class="text_exposed_root"&gt;&lt;p&gt;112 lovely 5 star reviews already! Many thanks to everyone who takes the time to review their visit. It means a lot to the volunteers and is also of great help to other visitors to the area trying to decide what to do and where to go!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; A lovely visit to the Highland Titles Nature Reserve&lt;br /&gt; 5 of 5 stars&lt;br /&gt; While on holiday in Scotland recently we visited the Highland Titles Nature Reserve to visit our plots of land and to see the conservation work being done there. I had arranged &lt;span class="text_exposed_hide"&gt;...&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="text_exposed_show"&gt;the visit a few weeks before and when we arrived we were greeted by Stewart and David who took us for a ride in the buggy and showed us around the reserve. It was very interesting to learn about the work being done on the reserve and it&#039;s nice to know that the money raised from the sale of plots of land is being put to such good use. Our plots were a little way off the main pathway so Stewart took me to see where they were while David stayed in the buggy with my mother. We both thoroughly enjoyed the visit and hope to return again in the future.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;span class="text_exposed_hide"&gt; &lt;span class="text_exposed_link"&gt;&lt;a _ohf"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="mtm plm _5pcm"&gt;&lt;div class="mbs _11dd fwn fcg" data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;C&quot;&#125;"&gt;&lt;div class="_5pcn fwb" data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;k&quot;&#125;"&gt;&lt;a href="/scottishhighlandtitles/videos/920350461344932/?fref=nf"&gt;Highland Titles&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="mtm _5pco" data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;K&quot;&#125;"&gt;&lt;div id="id_558b461fc08027891561199" class="text_exposed_root"&gt;&lt;p&gt;A lovely daytime capture of a Roe Deer up at the No:4 Lure stick. Still not a whisker of a Wildcat spotted, but we&#039;re still looking &lt;i class="_4-k1 img sp_fM-mz8spZ1b sx_7f72ac"&gt;&lt;u&gt;wink emoticon&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; Mating season &lt;span class="text_exposed_hide"&gt;...&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="text_exposed_show"&gt;for roe deer is in July and August. At this time, bucks chase does around prominent features such as a tree or large rock. This produces circles or figure-of-eight patterns of flattened vegetation, known as roe deer rings.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="text_exposed_show"&gt;&lt;p&gt; By the 1700s, the north of Scotland was the only part of Britain where native roe deer survived. Since then, re-introductions in many places and the cover provided by new plantations have allowed roe to spread and thrive.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; The most likely places to see a roe deer are often at the fringe of woods, where trees meet fields or moorland, or along quiet woodland paths. Early morning and dusk are good times. data-ft="&#123;&quot;tn&quot;:&quot;K&quot;&#125;"&gt;&lt;p&gt;A couple of night captures of a young pine marten...&lt;br /&gt; Gorgeous in its chocolate and yellow-buff fur and nimble as a squirrel when it moves, the pine marten is an ace tree-climbing predator. Its becoming more widespread again in Scotland after near-extinction, but is always scattered in small numbers and hard to see.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;div real Christmas gift. It was very cold, but sure worth the visit. We were driven around in the buggy and the views were stunning! We learned a lot about the reserve. It&#039;s a delight to meet volunteers, that find so much passion in their work and want to share this passion with the visitors.
